﻿using Microsoft.AspNetCore.Components;
using MudBlazor.State;
using MudBlazor.Utilities;

namespace MudBlazor
{
    /// <summary>
    /// A selectable option displayed within a <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/> component.
    /// </summary>
    /// <typeparam name="T">The type of value linked to this item.  Must be the same type as the parent <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/>.</typeparam>
    /// <seealso cref="MudSelect{T}"/>
    public partial class MudSelectItem<T> : MudComponentBase, IDisposable
    {
        private MudSelectContext<T>? _context;
        private MudSelectContext<T>? _shadowContext;
        private IDisposable? _selectionSubscription;

        private string GetCssClasses() => new CssBuilder()
            .AddClass(Class)
            .Build();

        internal string ItemId { get; } = Identifier.Create();

        /// <summary>
        /// Builds fallback accessibility attributes for the rendered option element.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// Option semantics come from this item's selection state rather than the popup's temporary active item.
        /// </remarks>
        private Dictionary<string, object?> GetUserAttributes()
        {
            var attributes = new Dictionary<string, object?>(UserAttributes, StringComparer.OrdinalIgnoreCase);
            attributes.TryAdd("aria-selected", Selected ? "true" : "false");

            if (Disabled)
            {
                attributes.TryAdd("aria-disabled", "true");
            }

            return attributes;
        }

        public MudSelectItem()
        {
            using var registerScope = CreateRegisterScope();
            registerScope.RegisterParameter<IMudSelect?>(nameof(IMudSelect))
                .WithParameter(() => IMudSelect)
                .WithChangeHandler(OnMudSelectChanged);
            registerScope.RegisterParameter<IMudShadowSelect?>(nameof(IMudShadowSelect))
                .WithParameter(() => IMudShadowSelect)
                .WithChangeHandler(OnMudShadowSelectChanged);
            registerScope.RegisterParameter<T?>(nameof(Value))
                .WithParameter(() => Value)
                .WithChangeHandler(OnValueChanged)
                .WithComparer(() => (_context ?? _shadowContext)?.Comparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default);
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// The <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/> hosting this item.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// This cascading parameter is used to obtain the context for registration.
        /// When this parameter changes, OnMudSelectChanged is invoked to handle
        /// registration and unregistration with the appropriate parent.
        /// </remarks>
        [CascadingParameter]
        internal IMudSelect? IMudSelect { get; set; }

        /// <summary>
        /// The shadow select used for items that only provide RenderFragments.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// Shadow items (HideContent=true) are registered in a separate lookup
        /// for value-to-RenderFragment resolution when the dropdown is closed.
        /// </remarks>
        [CascadingParameter]
        internal IMudShadowSelect? IMudShadowSelect { get; set; }

        /// <summary>
        /// Select items with HideContent==true are only there to register their RenderFragment with the select but
        /// won't render and have no other purpose!
        /// </summary>
        [CascadingParameter(Name = "HideContent")]
        internal bool HideContent { get; set; }

        /// <summary>
        /// Gets the parent MudSelect component.
        /// </summary>
        internal MudSelect<T>? MudSelect => (MudSelect<T>?)IMudSelect;

        /// <summary>
        /// The custom value associated with this item.
        /// </summary>
        [Parameter]
        [Category(CategoryTypes.FormComponent.Behavior)]
        public T? Value { get; set; }

        /// <summary>
        /// Prevents the user from interacting with this item.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// Defaults to <c>false</c>.
        /// </remarks>
        [Parameter]
        [Category(CategoryTypes.General.Behavior)]
        public bool Disabled { get; set; }

        /// <summary>
        /// The custom content within this item.
        /// </summary>
        [Parameter]
        [Category(CategoryTypes.General.Behavior)]
        public RenderFragment? ChildContent { get; set; }

        /// <summary>
        /// Whether multi-selection is enabled in the parent <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/>.
        /// </summary>
        protected bool MultiSelection => _context?.MultiSelection == true;

        /// <summary>
        /// Whether this item is selected.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// <para>
        /// This state is updated by observing the parent's selection via the context.
        /// Items subscribe to selection changes and update this state accordingly.
        /// </para>
        /// </remarks>
        internal bool Selected { get; set; }

        /// <summary>
        /// The icon to display whether this item is selected.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// When <see cref="Selected"/> is <c>true</c>, <see cref="Icons.Material.Filled.CheckBox"/> is returned.  Otherwise, <see cref="Icons.Material.Filled.CheckBoxOutlineBlank"/>.
        /// </remarks>
        protected string? CheckBoxIcon
        {
            get
            {
                if (!MultiSelection)
                    return null;
                return Selected ? Icons.Material.Filled.CheckBox : Icons.Material.Filled.CheckBoxOutlineBlank;
            }
        }

        protected string DisplayString
        {
            get
            {
                // Use the parent's ConvertValueToString which delegates to ConvertSet (handles ToStringFunc)
                return MudSelect?.ConvertValueToString(Value) ?? $"{Value}";
            }
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Handles changes to the IMudShadowSelect cascading parameter.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// This is invoked when the shadow select parent changes (e.g., when moving between different selects).
        /// It unregisters from the old parent and registers with the new one.
        /// </remarks>
        private void OnMudShadowSelectChanged(ParameterChangedEventArgs<IMudShadowSelect?> args)
        {
            if (args.LastValue?.SelectContext is MudSelectContext<T> oldContext)
            {
                oldContext.UnregisterShadowItem(this);
            }

            if (args.Value?.SelectContext is MudSelectContext<T> newContext)
            {
                _shadowContext = newContext;
                _shadowContext.RegisterShadowItem(this);
            }
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Handles changes to the IMudSelect cascading parameter.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// <para>
        /// This is invoked when the select parent changes (e.g., when moving between different selects).
        /// It handles the complete lifecycle:
        /// </para>
        /// <list type="number">
        /// <item><description>Unsubscribes from the old parent's selection changes</description></item>
        /// <item><description>Unregisters from the old parent's context</description></item>
        /// <item><description>Registers with the new parent's context</description></item>
        /// <item><description>Subscribes to the new parent's selection changes</description></item>
        /// <item><description>Updates the initial Selected state</description></item>
        /// </list>
        /// </remarks>
        private void OnMudSelectChanged(ParameterChangedEventArgs<IMudSelect?> args)
        {
            if (args.LastValue?.SelectContext is MudSelectContext<T> oldContext)
            {
                _selectionSubscription?.Dispose();
                _selectionSubscription = null;
                oldContext.UnregisterItem(this);
            }

            if (args.Value?.SelectContext is MudSelectContext<T> newContext)
            {
                _context = newContext;

                // Register as a visible item (adds to _items, _valueLookup, and _shadowLookup)
                var isSelected = _context.RegisterItem(this);
                Selected = isSelected;

                _selectionSubscription = _context.SubscribeToSelectionChanges(OnSelectionChangedAsync);
            }
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Handles selection changes from the parent select.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// This callback is invoked when the parent's SelectedValues changes.
        /// It updates the local Selected state and triggers a re-render if needed.
        /// This replaces the OnUpdateSelectionStateFromOutside method.
        /// </remarks>
        private Task OnSelectionChangedAsync(IReadOnlyCollection<T?> selectedValues)
        {
            var oldSelected = Selected;
            Selected = selectedValues.Contains(Value);

            if (oldSelected != Selected)
            {
                // Avoid await InvokeAsync(StateHasChanged) due to a MAUI dispatcher bug:
                // https://github.com/MudBlazor/MudBlazor/issues/13009
                // This issue does not occur on other platforms (e.g., WASM, WinForms Hybrid, etc).
                StateHasChanged();
            }

            return Task.CompletedTask;
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Handles changes to the <see cref="Value"/> parameter.
        /// </summary>
        /// <remarks>
        /// When the parent swaps the underlying data collection while Blazor reuses the same component instances
        /// (e.g. a keyless <c>@foreach</c> binding new items to existing <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}"/> positions),
        /// the value-keyed lookups in <see cref="MudSelectContext{T}"/> must be updated to avoid stale keys.
        /// </remarks>
        private void OnValueChanged(ParameterChangedEventArgs<T?> args)
        {
            _context?.OnItemValueChanged(this, args.LastValue, args.Value);
            _shadowContext?.OnShadowItemValueChanged(this, args.LastValue, args.Value);
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Handles click events on the item.
        /// </summary>
        private async Task OnClickHandleAsync()
        {
            if (MudSelect is not null)
            {
                await MudSelect.SelectOption(Value);
            }
        }

        /// <inheritdoc />
        public void Dispose()
        {
            Dispose(true);
            GC.SuppressFinalize(this);
        }

        /// <summary>
        /// Releases resources used by this component.
        /// </summary>
        protected virtual void Dispose(bool disposing)
        {
            if (!disposing)
            {
                return;
            }

            var selection = _selectionSubscription;
            var context = _context;
            var shadow = _shadowContext;

            _selectionSubscription = null;
            _context = null;
            _shadowContext = null;

            selection?.Dispose();
            context?.UnregisterItem(this);
            shadow?.UnregisterShadowItem(this);
        }
    }
}

2026-05-29 16:05:41,001 - INFO - swea-agent-MudBlazor__MudBlazor-13109 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the issue fully. Let me trace through the code path:

1. When a `MudSelect<T>` has a custom `Comparer`, it's used in many places for comparing values.
2. However, the `MudSelectContext<T>` uses dictionaries with `NullableObject<T?>` keys, and `NullableObject<T?>` uses `EqualityComparer<T?>.Default` for equality/hash code - NOT the custom comparer.
3. When `SelectedValues` is set with initial items, the `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` method updates `_selectedValues` (a `HashSet<T?>`) using the custom comparer. But the lookup in `CanRenderValue` and `GetSelectedValuePresenter` relies on `_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue` which uses the dictionary that doesn't use the custom comparer.

Wait, but the test `MultiSelectWithCustomComparer` seems to pass. Let me look more carefully at the PR description. The issue is specifically about:
1. `Comparer` parameter set
2. Initial items in `SelectedValues` bound collection

Let me look at the snippet links mentioned in the PR. The first one is about a deadlock, the second one shows that "test1" is not selected.

Let me look at how the `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` works and trace the problem more carefully.

The key issue: In `MudSelectContext`, the dictionaries `_valueLookup` and `_shadowLookup` are keyed by `NullableObject<T?>`. The `NullableObject<T?>` uses `EqualityComparer<T?>.Default.Equals` and `EqualityComparer<T>.Default.GetHashCode()`. When a user provides a custom `Comparer`, these dictionaries won't respect it. So:

- When you have initial `SelectedValues` with items that are "equal" according to the custom comparer but not according to the default comparer, the lookup `TryGetShadowItemByValue` will fail to find the matching item.
- This causes `CanRenderValue` to return `false` (because `_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue` fails), so no value is rendered.

But wait, the test `MultiSelectWithCustomComparer` works... Let me check - it uses `SetSelection` button click, not initial values. Let me look more carefully at the flow.

Actually, looking at the `MultiSelectWithCustomComparerTest`, it sets values via a button click (`SetSelection`), not as initial values. The issue in the PR description says initial items in `SelectedValues` cause the problem.

Let me look at the `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` method more carefully:

```csharp
private async Task OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync(ParameterChangedEventArgs<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>?> arg)
{
    var value = arg.Value;
    _selectedValues = value != null ? new HashSet<T?>(value, Comparer) : new HashSet<T?>(Comparer);
    await _context.NotifySelectionChangedAsync();

    if (!MultiSelection)
    {
        await SetValueAndUpdateTextAsync(_selectedValues.FirstOrDefault());
    }
    ...
}
```

The `SetValueAndUpdateTextAsync` sets the `Value` property. But later when rendering, `CanRenderValue` checks:

```csharp
protected bool CanRenderValue
{
    get
    {
        if (MultiSelection) return false;
        if (ToStringFunc is not null && !string.IsNullOrEmpty(ToStringFunc(ReadValue))) return false;
        if (!_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue(ReadValue, out var item)) return false;
        return item.ChildContent != null;
    }
}
```

The `TryGetShadowItemByValue` uses the dictionary with `NullableObject<T?>` keys that don't respect custom comparer. So if `ReadValue` is an object that's "equal" to an item's value via custom comparer but not via default equality, this fails.

But wait, there's another issue. Let me check the `IsValueInList` property:

```csharp
protected bool IsValueInList => _context.TryGetShadowItemByValue(ReadValue, out _);
```

And `GetSelectedValuePresenter`:

```csharp
protected RenderFragment? GetSelectedValuePresenter()
{
    if (!_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue(ReadValue, out var item)) return null;
    return item.ChildContent;
}
```

These all use `_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue` which doesn't respect the custom comparer.

Now, the fix should make the dictionaries in `MudSelectContext` use the custom comparer from the parent `MudSelect`. Let me check if `MudSelectContext` has access to the comparer:

Yes, it does:
```csharp
public IEqualityComparer<T?>? Comparer => _select.Comparer;
```

But the dictionaries are created with default constructors:
```csharp
private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _valueLookup = new();
private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _shadowLookup = new();
```

These need to be constructed with a custom `IEqualityComparer<NullableObject<T?>>` that wraps the user's comparer.

Let me now create a reproduce script.

﻿// Copyright (c) MudBlazor 2021
// MudBlazor licenses this file to you under the MIT license.
// See the LICENSE file in the project root for more information.

namespace MudBlazor.Utilities.Comparer;


/// <summary>
/// Compares two sequences element-by-element using a specified element comparer.
/// </summary>
/// <typeparam name="T">The type of elements in the sequences.</typeparam>
internal class SequenceComparer<T> : IEqualityComparer<IEnumerable<T?>?>
{
    private readonly IEqualityComparer<T?> _elementComparer;

    /// <summary>
    /// Initializes a new instance of the <see cref="SequenceComparer{T}"/> class.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="elementComparer">The comparer to use for individual elements. If null, uses the default comparer.</param>
    public SequenceComparer(IEqualityComparer<T?>? elementComparer = null)
    {
        _elementComparer = elementComparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default;
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Determines whether two sequences are equal by comparing each element.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="x">The first sequence to compare.</param>
    /// <param name="y">The second sequence to compare.</param>
    /// <returns>True if the sequences are equal; otherwise, false.</returns>
    public bool Equals(IEnumerable<T?>? x, IEnumerable<T?>? y)
    {
        if (ReferenceEquals(x, y)) return true;
        if (x is null || y is null) return false;

        return x.SequenceEqual(y, _elementComparer);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Returns a hash code for the specified sequence.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="obj">The sequence for which to get a hash code.</param>
    /// <returns>A hash code for the sequence.</returns>
    public int GetHashCode(IEnumerable<T?>? obj)
    {
        if (obj is null) return 0;

        unchecked
        {
            var hash = 17;
            foreach (var item in obj)
            {
                hash = (hash * 31) + (item is null ? 0 : _elementComparer.GetHashCode(item));
            }

            return hash;
        }
    }
}

This sets `_selectedValues` using the custom comparer.\n3. For non-multi-select, it calls `SetValueAndUpdateTextAsync(_selectedValues.FirstOrDefault())` which sets the `Value` property.\n4. Later during rendering, `CanRenderValue` checks if `_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue(ReadValue, out var item)` - this uses the dictionary which doesn't respect the custom comparer.\n5. If the value object is not the same reference, the lookup fails, and `CanRenderValue` returns `false`, causing the input to display nothing.\n\nBut wait, there's another potential issue. Let me look at the test more closely. I need to check if there are tests that specifically test the comparer with initial values. Let me also check the PR description again - it mentions two snippets. Let me understand what exactly the bug is.

Looking at the code flow:

1. When `MudSelect` has `Comparer` set and `SelectedValues` has initial items, `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` is called.
2. This sets `_selectedValues` using the custom comparer.
3. For non-multi-select, it calls `SetValueAndUpdateTextAsync(_selectedValues.FirstOrDefault())` which sets the `Value` property.
4. Later during rendering, `CanRenderValue` checks if `_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue(ReadValue, out var item)` - this uses the dictionary which doesn't respect the custom comparer.
5. If the value object is not the same reference, the lookup fails, and `CanRenderValue` returns `false`, causing the input to display nothing.

But wait, there's another potential issue. Let me look at `RegisterItem` in `MudSelectContext`:

```csharp
public bool RegisterItem(MudSelectItem<T> item)
{
    if (!_items.Contains(item))
    {
        _items.Add(item);
    }
    _valueLookup[item.Value] = item;

    return _select.MultiSelection switch
    {
        true => _select.GetSelectedValues()?.Contains(item.Value) == true,
        false => _select.ReadValue?.Equals(item.Value) == true
    };
}
```

Here, for single selection, `_select.ReadValue?.Equals(item.Value)` uses the default `Equals` method of the object, not the custom comparer! This means the initial selection state won't be correct either.

Also, in `MudSelectItem.razor.cs`, the `OnSelectionChangedAsync`:

```csharp
private Task OnSelectionChangedAsync(IReadOnlyCollection<T?> selectedValues)
{
    var oldSelected = Selected;
    Selected = selectedValues.Contains(Value);
    ...
}
```

`selectedValues.Contains(Value)` - the `IReadOnlyCollection<T?>` is actually a `HashSet<T?>` that was created with the custom comparer. So this should work correctly for the selection notification.

But the initial `RegisterItem` check uses `_select.ReadValue?.Equals(item.Value)` which doesn't use the custom comparer!

Now let me think about the solution. The core issue is that:
1. `MudSelectContext` dictionaries use `NullableObject<T?>` as keys, which uses default equality.
2. `RegisterItem` uses `_select.ReadValue?.Equals(item.Value)` for single selection.

The fix should:
1. Make `MudSelectContext`'s dictionaries use the custom comparer from the parent `MudSelect`.
2. Fix `RegisterItem` to use the custom comparer for single selection.

using System.Diagnostics.CodeAnalysis;
using MudBlazor.Extensions;
using MudBlazor.Interfaces;
using MudBlazor.Utilities;

namespace MudBlazor;

/// <summary>
/// Manages the communication between <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/> and <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}"/> components.
/// </summary>
/// <typeparam name="T">The type of value being selected.</typeparam>
internal sealed class MudSelectContext<T>
{
    private readonly MudSelect<T> _select;
    private readonly List<MudSelectItem<T>> _items = [];
    private readonly List<Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task>> _selectionObservers = [];
    private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _valueLookup;
    private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _shadowLookup;

    /// <summary>
    /// Initializes a new instance of the <see cref="MudSelectContext{T}"/> class.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="select">The parent select component.</param>
    public MudSelectContext(MudSelect<T> select)
    {
        _select = select;
        var comparer = new NullableObjectComparer(select.Comparer);
        _valueLookup = new Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>>(comparer);
        _shadowLookup = new Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>>(comparer);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// An <see cref="IEqualityComparer{T}"/> for <see cref="NullableObject{T}"/> that delegates to the user-provided comparer.
    /// </summary>
    private sealed class NullableObjectComparer : IEqualityComparer<NullableObject<T?>>
    {
        private readonly IEqualityComparer<T?> _elementComparer;

        public NullableObjectComparer(IEqualityComparer<T?>? elementComparer)
        {
            _elementComparer = elementComparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default;
        }

        public bool Equals(NullableObject<T?> x, NullableObject<T?> y)
        {
            if (x.IsNull && y.IsNull)
            {
                return true;
            }

            if (x.IsNull || y.IsNull)
            {
                return false;
            }

            return _elementComparer.Equals(x.Item, y.Item);
        }

        public int GetHashCode(NullableObject<T?> obj)
        {
            if (obj.IsNull)
            {
                return 0;
            }

            return _elementComparer.GetHashCode(obj.Item);
        }
    }'

So I need a different approach. Options:
1. Make the `NullableObjectComparer` hold a reference to the `MudSelect` and delegate to its `Comparer` property dynamically.
2. Rebuild the dictionaries when `Comparer` changes.
3. Fix the lookup methods to iterate through the dictionary values (or maintain a separate list) and use the custom comparer.

Option 1 seems cleanest:

﻿// Copyright (c) MudBlazor 2021
// MudBlazor licenses this file to you under the MIT license.
// See the LICENSE file in the project root for more information.

using System.Diagnostics.CodeAnalysis;
using MudBlazor.Extensions;
using MudBlazor.Interfaces;
using MudBlazor.Utilities;

namespace MudBlazor;

/// <summary>
/// Manages the communication between <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/> and <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}"/> components.
/// </summary>
/// <typeparam name="T">The type of value being selected.</typeparam>
internal sealed class MudSelectContext<T>
{
    private readonly MudSelect<T> _select;
    private readonly List<MudSelectItem<T>> _items = [];
    private readonly List<Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task>> _selectionObservers = [];
    private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _valueLookup = new();
    private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _shadowLookup = new();

    /// <summary>
    /// Initializes a new instance of the <see cref="MudSelectContext{T}"/> class.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="select">The parent select component.</param>
    public MudSelectContext(MudSelect<T> select)
    {
        _select = select;
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets the ordered list of all visible items in the dropdown.
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Exposed as List to support FindIndex operations in the parent component.
    /// </remarks>
    public IReadOnlyList<MudSelectItem<T>> Items => _items;

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets all shadow items (including both visible and hidden items).
    /// </summary>
    public IReadOnlyCollection<MudSelectItem<T>> ShadowItems => _shadowLookup.Values;

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets whether multi-selection is enabled.
    /// </summary>
    public bool MultiSelection => _select.MultiSelection;

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets the current selected values.
    /// </summary>
    public IReadOnlyCollection<T?> SelectedValues => _select.GetSelectedValues() ?? Array.Empty<T?>();

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets the user-supplied value comparer from the parent <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/>, if any.
    /// </summary>
    public IEqualityComparer<T?>? Comparer => _select.Comparer;

    /// <summary>
    /// Registers an item as visible in the dropdown list.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="item">The item to register.</param>
    /// <returns><c>true</c> if the item is currently selected; otherwise <c>false</c>.</returns>
    public bool RegisterItem(MudSelectItem<T> item)
    {
        // Add to the ordered list of visible items
        if (!_items.Contains(item))
        {
            _items.Add(item);
        }

        // Add to value lookup for fast access by value
        _valueLookup[item.Value] = item;

        // Note: Do NOT add to _shadowLookup here - that's only for shadow items
        // Shadow items are registered separately via RegisterShadowItem

        // Check if this item's value is currently selected
        return _select.MultiSelection switch
        {
            true => _select.GetSelectedValues()?.Contains(item.Value) == true,
            false => _select.ReadValue?.Equals(item.Value) == true
        };
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Unregisters an item from the dropdown list.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="item">The item to unregister.</param>
    public void UnregisterItem(MudSelectItem<T> item)
    {
        _items.Remove(item);
        _valueLookup.Remove(item.Value);
        // Note: Do NOT remove from _shadowLookup - that's managed by shadow items
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Registers an item for value-to-RenderFragment lookup only (not visible in dropdown).
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Used for items with HideContent=true that provide RenderFragments for selected values
    /// that may not be in the visible dropdown list.
    /// </remarks>
    /// <param name="item">The item to register.</param>
    public void RegisterShadowItem(MudSelectItem<T>? item)
    {
        if (item is null)
        {
            return;
        }

        _shadowLookup[item.Value] = item;
        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Unregisters a shadow item.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="item">The item to unregister.</param>
    public void UnregisterShadowItem(MudSelectItem<T>? item)
    {
        if (item is null)
        {
            return;
        }

        _shadowLookup.Remove(item.Value);
        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Updates the visible-item lookup when a registered item's <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.Value"/> parameter changes.
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    /// The lookup is keyed by value captured at registration time. When the value parameter is later mutated
    /// (e.g. the parent swaps the underlying data collection while reusing the same component instances),
    /// the old key would otherwise point to a stale <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}"/> reference and the new value
    /// would not be found at all.
    /// </remarks>
    public void OnItemValueChanged(MudSelectItem<T> item, T? oldValue, T? newValue)
    {
        var oldKey = new NullableObject<T?>(oldValue);
        if (_valueLookup.TryGetValue(oldKey, out var existing) && ReferenceEquals(existing, item))
        {
            _valueLookup.Remove(oldKey);
        }

        _valueLookup[newValue] = item;
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Updates the shadow lookup when a registered shadow item's <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.Value"/> parameter changes.
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Also requests a re-render of the parent <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/>: <c>GetSelectedValuePresenter</c> runs
    /// during the parent's render pass, before child <c>SetParametersAsync</c> has propagated the new value,
    /// so a second render is needed for the correct <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.ChildContent"/> to be emitted.
    /// </remarks>
    public void OnShadowItemValueChanged(MudSelectItem<T> item, T? oldValue, T? newValue)
    {
        var oldKey = new NullableObject<T?>(oldValue);
        if (_shadowLookup.TryGetValue(oldKey, out var existing) && ReferenceEquals(existing, item))
        {
            _shadowLookup.Remove(oldKey);
        }

        _shadowLookup[newValue] = item;
        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
        ((IMudStateHasChanged)_select).StateHasChanged();
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Attempts to get an item by its value from visible items.
    /// </summary>
    public bool TryGetItemByValue(T? value, [NotNullWhen(true)] out MudSelectItem<T>? item)
    {
        return _valueLookup.TryGetValue(value, out item);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Attempts to get an item by its value from all items (including shadow items).
    /// </summary>
    public bool TryGetShadowItemByValue(T? value, [NotNullWhen(true)] out MudSelectItem<T>? item)
    {
        return _shadowLookup.TryGetValue(value, out item);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Subscribes to selection changes.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="observer">The callback to invoke when selection changes.</param>
    /// <returns>A disposable subscription that can be used to unsubscribe.</returns>
    public IDisposable SubscribeToSelectionChanges(Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
    {
        _selectionObservers.Add(observer);
        return new SelectionSubscription(this, observer);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Unsubscribes an observer from selection changes.
    /// </summary>
    private void Unsubscribe(Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
    {
        _selectionObservers.Remove(observer);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Notifies all observers of a selection change.
    /// </summary>
    public async Task NotifySelectionChangedAsync()
    {
        var selectedValues = SelectedValues;
        for (var i = _selectionObservers.Count - 1; i >= 0; i--)
        {
            await _selectionObservers[i](selectedValues);
        }
    }

    private sealed class SelectionSubscription(MudSelectContext<T> context, Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
        : IDisposable
    {
        private MudSelectContext<T>? _context = context;
        private Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task>? _observer = observer;

        public void Dispose()
        {
            var contextCopy = _context;
            var observerCopy = _observer;

            if (contextCopy is null || observerCopy is null)
            {
                return;
            }

            _context = null;
            _observer = null;

            contextCopy.Unsubscribe(observerCopy);
        }
    }
}

OBSERVATION:

     1	﻿// Copyright (c) MudBlazor 2021
     2	// MudBlazor licenses this file to you under the MIT license.
     3	// See the LICENSE file in the project root for more information.
     4	
     5	using System.Diagnostics.CodeAnalysis;
     6	using MudBlazor.Extensions;
     7	using MudBlazor.Interfaces;
     8	using MudBlazor.Utilities;
     9	
    10	namespace MudBlazor;
    11	
    12	/// <summary>
    13	/// Manages the communication between <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/> and <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}"/> components.
    14	/// </summary>
    15	/// <typeparam name="T">The type of value being selected.</typeparam>
    16	internal sealed class MudSelectContext<T>
    17	{
    18	    private readonly MudSelect<T> _select;
    19	    private readonly List<MudSelectItem<T>> _items = [];
    20	    private readonly List<Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task>> _selectionObservers = [];
    21	    private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _valueLookup = new();
    22	    private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _shadowLookup = new();
    23	
    24	    /// <summary>
    25	    /// Initializes a new instance of the <see cref="MudSelectContext{T}"/> class.
    26	    /// </summary>
    27	    /// <param name="select">The parent select component.</param>
    28	    public MudSelectContext(MudSelect<T> select)
    29	    {
    30	        _select = select;
    31	    }
    32	
    33	    /// <summary>
    34	    /// Gets the ordered list of all visible items in the dropdown.
    35	    /// </summary>
    36	    /// <remarks>
    37	    /// Exposed as List to support FindIndex operations in the parent component.
    38	    /// </remarks>
    39	    public IReadOnlyList<MudSelectItem<T>> Items => _items;
    40	
    41	    /// <summary>
    42	    /// Gets all shadow items (including both visible and hidden items).
    43	    /// </summary>
    44	    public IReadOnlyCollection<MudSelectItem<T>> ShadowItems => _shadowLookup.Values;
    45	
    46	    /// <summary>
    47	    /// Gets whether multi-selection is enabled.
    48	    /// </summary>
    49	    public bool MultiSelection => _select.MultiSelection;
    50	
    51	    /// <summary>
    52	    /// Gets the current selected values.
    53	    /// </summary>
    54	    public IReadOnlyCollection<T?> SelectedValues => _select.GetSelectedValues() ?? Array.Empty<T?>();
    55	
    56	    /// <summary>
    57	    /// Gets the user-supplied value comparer from the parent <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/>, if any.
    58	    /// </summary>
    59	    public IEqualityComparer<T?>? Comparer => _select.Comparer;
    60	
    61	    /// <summary>
    62	    /// Registers an item as visible in the dropdown list.
    63	    /// </summary>
    64	    /// <param name="item">The item to register.</param>
    65	    /// <returns><c>true</c> if the item is currently selected; otherwise <c>false</c>.</returns>
    66	    public bool RegisterItem(MudSelectItem<T> item)
    67	    {
    68	        // Add to the ordered list of visible items
    69	        if (!_items.Contains(item))
    70	        {
    71	            _items.Add(item);
    72	        }
    73	
    74	        // Add to value lookup for fast access by value
    75	        _valueLookup[item.Value] = item;
    76	
    77	        // Note: Do NOT add to _shadowLookup here - that's only for shadow items
    78	        // Shadow items are registered separately via RegisterShadowItem
    79	
    80	        // Check if this item's value is currently selected
    81	        return _select.MultiSelection switch
    82	        {
    83	            true => _select.GetSelectedValues()?.Contains(item.Value) == true,
    84	            false => _select.ReadValue?.Equals(item.Value) == true
    85	        };
    86	    }
    87	
    88	    /// <summary>
    89	    /// Unregisters an item from the dropdown list.
    90	    /// </summary>
    91	    /// <param name="item">The item to unregister.</param>
    92	    public void UnregisterItem(MudSelectItem<T> item)
    93	    {
    94	        _items.Remove(item);
    95	        _valueLookup.Remove(item.Value);
    96	        // Note: Do NOT remove from _shadowLookup - that's managed by shadow items
    97	    }
    98	
    99	    /// <summary>
   100	    /// Registers an item for value-to-RenderFragment lookup only (not visible in dropdown).
   101	    /// </summary>
   102	    /// <remarks>
   103	    /// Used for items with HideContent=true that provide RenderFragments for selected values
   104	    /// that may not be in the visible dropdown list.
   105	    /// </remarks>
   106	    /// <param name="item">The item to register.</param>
   107	    public void RegisterShadowItem(MudSelectItem<T>? item)
   108	    {
   109	        if (item is null)
   110	        {
   111	            return;
   112	        }
   113	
   114	        _shadowLookup[item.Value] = item;
   115	        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
   116	    }
   117	
   118	    /// <summary>
   119	    /// Unregisters a shadow item.
   120	    /// </summary>
   121	    /// <param name="item">The item to unregister.</param>
   122	    public void UnregisterShadowItem(MudSelectItem<T>? item)
   123	    {
   124	        if (item is null)
   125	        {
   126	            return;
   127	        }
   128	
   129	        _shadowLookup.Remove(item.Value);
   130	        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
   131	    }
   132	
   133	    /// <summary>
   134	    /// Updates the visible-item lookup when a registered item's <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.Value"/> parameter changes.
   135	    /// </summary>
   136	    /// <remarks>
   137	    /// The lookup is keyed by value captured at registration time. When the value parameter is later mutated
   138	    /// (e.g. the parent swaps the underlying data collection while reusing the same component instances),
   139	    /// the old key would otherwise point to a stale <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}"/> reference and the new value
   140	    /// would not be found at all.
   141	    /// </remarks>
   142	    public void OnItemValueChanged(MudSelectItem<T> item, T? oldValue, T? newValue)
   143	    {
   144	        var oldKey = new NullableObject<T?>(oldValue);
   145	        if (_valueLookup.TryGetValue(oldKey, out var existing) && ReferenceEquals(existing, item))
   146	        {
   147	            _valueLookup.Remove(oldKey);
   148	        }
   149	
   150	        _valueLookup[newValue] = item;
   151	    }
   152	
   153	    /// <summary>
   154	    /// Updates the shadow lookup when a registered shadow item's <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.Value"/> parameter changes.
   155	    /// </summary>
   156	    /// <remarks>
   157	    /// Also requests a re-render of the parent <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/>: <c>GetSelectedValuePresenter</c> runs
   158	    /// during the parent's render pass, before child <c>SetParametersAsync</c> has propagated the new value,
   159	    /// so a second render is needed for the correct <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.ChildContent"/> to be emitted.
   160	    /// </remarks>
   161	    public void OnShadowItemValueChanged(MudSelectItem<T> item, T? oldValue, T? newValue)
   162	    {
   163	        var oldKey = new NullableObject<T?>(oldValue);
   164	        if (_shadowLookup.TryGetValue(oldKey, out var existing) && ReferenceEquals(existing, item))
   165	        {
   166	            _shadowLookup.Remove(oldKey);
   167	        }
   168	
   169	        _shadowLookup[newValue] = item;
   170	        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
   171	        ((IMudStateHasChanged)_select).StateHasChanged();
   172	    }
   173	
   174	    /// <summary>
   175	    /// Attempts to get an item by its value from visible items.
   176	    /// </summary>
   177	    public bool TryGetItemByValue(T? value, [NotNullWhen(true)] out MudSelectItem<T>? item)
   178	    {
   179	        return _valueLookup.TryGetValue(value, out item);
   180	    }
   181	
   182	    /// <summary>
   183	    /// Attempts to get an item by its value from all items (including shadow items).
   184	    /// </summary>
   185	    public bool TryGetShadowItemByValue(T? value, [NotNullWhen(true)] out MudSelectItem<T>? item)
   186	    {
   187	        return _shadowLookup.TryGetValue(value, out item);
   188	    }
   189	
   190	    /// <summary>
   191	    /// Subscribes to selection changes.
   192	    /// </summary>
   193	    /// <param name="observer">The callback to invoke when selection changes.</param>
   194	    /// <returns>A disposable subscription that can be used to unsubscribe.</returns>
   195	    public IDisposable SubscribeToSelectionChanges(Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
   196	    {
   197	        _selectionObservers.Add(observer);
   198	        return new SelectionSubscription(this, observer);
   199	    }
   200	
   201	    /// <summary>
   202	    /// Unsubscribes an observer from selection changes.
   203	    /// </summary>
   204	    private void Unsubscribe(Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
   205	    {
   206	        _selectionObservers.Remove(observer);
   207	    }
   208	
   209	    /// <summary>
   210	    /// Notifies all observers of a selection change.
   211	    /// </summary>
   212	    public async Task NotifySelectionChangedAsync()
   213	    {
   214	        var selectedValues = SelectedValues;
   215	        for (var i = _selectionObservers.Count - 1; i >= 0; i--)
   216	        {
   217	            await _selectionObservers[i](selectedValues);
   218	        }
   219	    }
   220	
   221	    private sealed class SelectionSubscription(MudSelectContext<T> context, Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
   222	        : IDisposable
   223	    {
   224	        private MudSelectContext<T>? _context = context;
   225	        private Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task>? _observer = observer;
   226	
   227	        public void Dispose()
   228	        {
   229	            var contextCopy = _context;
   230	            var observerCopy = _observer;
   231	
   232	            if (contextCopy is null || observerCopy is null)
   233	            {
   234	                return;
   235	            }
   236	
   237	            _context = null;
   238	            _observer = null;
   239	
   240	            contextCopy.Unsubscribe(observerCopy);
   241	        }
   242	    }
   243	}

// Copyright (c) MudBlazor 2021
// MudBlazor licenses this file to you under the MIT license.
// See the LICENSE file in the project root for more information.

using System.Diagnostics.CodeAnalysis;
using MudBlazor.Extensions;
using MudBlazor.Interfaces;
using MudBlazor.Utilities;

namespace MudBlazor;

/// <summary>
/// Manages the communication between <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/> and <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}"/> components.
/// </summary>
/// <typeparam name="T">The type of value being selected.</typeparam>
internal sealed class MudSelectContext<T>
{
    private readonly MudSelect<T> _select;
    private readonly List<MudSelectItem<T>> _items = [];
    private readonly List<Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task>> _selectionObservers = [];
    private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _valueLookup;
    private readonly Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>> _shadowLookup;

    /// <summary>
    /// Initializes a new instance of the <see cref="MudSelectContext{T}"/> class.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="select">The parent select component.</param>
    public MudSelectContext(MudSelect<T> select)
    {
        _select = select;
        var comparer = new NullableObjectComparer(select);
        _valueLookup = new Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>>(comparer);
        _shadowLookup = new Dictionary<NullableObject<T?>, MudSelectItem<T>>(comparer);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// An <see cref="IEqualityComparer{T}"/> for <see cref="NullableObject{T}"/> that delegates to the user-provided comparer.
    /// </summary>
    private sealed class NullableObjectComparer : IEqualityComparer<NullableObject<T?>>
    {
        private readonly MudSelect<T> _select;

        public NullableObjectComparer(MudSelect<T> select)
        {
            _select = select;
        }

        private IEqualityComparer<T?> ElementComparer => _select.Comparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default;

        public bool Equals(NullableObject<T?> x, NullableObject<T?> y)
        {
            if (x.IsNull && y.IsNull)
            {
                return true;
            }

            if (x.IsNull || y.IsNull)
            {
                return false;
            }

            return ElementComparer.Equals(x.Item, y.Item);
        }

        public int GetHashCode(NullableObject<T?> obj)
        {
            if (obj.IsNull)
            {
                return 0;
            }

            return ElementComparer.GetHashCode(obj.Item);
        }
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets the ordered list of all visible items in the dropdown.
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Exposed as List to support FindIndex operations in the parent component.
    /// </remarks>
    public IReadOnlyList<MudSelectItem<T>> Items => _items;

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets all shadow items (including both visible and hidden items).
    /// </summary>
    public IReadOnlyCollection<MudSelectItem<T>> ShadowItems => _shadowLookup.Values;

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets whether multi-selection is enabled.
    /// </summary>
    public bool MultiSelection => _select.MultiSelection;

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets the current selected values.
    /// </summary>
    public IReadOnlyCollection<T?> SelectedValues => _select.GetSelectedValues() ?? Array.Empty<T?>();

    /// <summary>
    /// Gets the user-supplied value comparer from the parent <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/>, if any.
    /// </summary>
    public IEqualityComparer<T?>? Comparer => _select.Comparer;

    /// <summary>
    /// Registers an item as visible in the dropdown list.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="item">The item to register.</param>
    /// <returns><c>true</c> if the item is currently selected; otherwise <c>false</c>.</returns>
    public bool RegisterItem(MudSelectItem<T> item)
    {
        // Add to the ordered list of visible items
        if (!_items.Contains(item))
        {
            _items.Add(item);
        }

        // Add to value lookup for fast access by value
        _valueLookup[item.Value] = item;

        // Note: Do NOT add to _shadowLookup here - that's only for shadow items
        // Shadow items are registered separately via RegisterShadowItem

        // Check if this item's value is currently selected
        var comparer = _select.Comparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default;
        return _select.MultiSelection switch
        {
            true => _select.GetSelectedValues()?.Contains(item.Value, comparer) == true,
            false => comparer.Equals(_select.ReadValue, item.Value)
        };
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Unregisters an item from the dropdown list.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="item">The item to unregister.</param>
    public void UnregisterItem(MudSelectItem<T> item)
    {
        _items.Remove(item);
        _valueLookup.Remove(item.Value);
        // Note: Do NOT remove from _shadowLookup - that's managed by shadow items
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Registers an item for value-to-RenderFragment lookup only (not visible in dropdown).
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Used for items with HideContent=true that provide RenderFragments for selected values
    /// that may not be in the visible dropdown list.
    /// </remarks>
    /// <param name="item">The item to register.</param>
    public void RegisterShadowItem(MudSelectItem<T>? item)
    {
        if (item is null)
        {
            return;
        }

        _shadowLookup[item.Value] = item;
        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Unregisters a shadow item.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="item">The item to unregister.</param>
    public void UnregisterShadowItem(MudSelectItem<T>? item)
    {
        if (item is null)
        {
            return;
        }

        _shadowLookup.Remove(item.Value);
        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Updates the visible-item lookup when a registered item's <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.Value"/> parameter changes.
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    /// The lookup is keyed by value captured at registration time. When the value parameter is later mutated
    /// (e.g. the parent swaps the underlying data collection while reusing the same component instances),
    /// the old key would otherwise point to a stale <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}"/> reference and the new value
    /// would not be found at all.
    /// </remarks>
    public void OnItemValueChanged(MudSelectItem<T> item, T? oldValue, T? newValue)
    {
        var oldKey = new NullableObject<T?>(oldValue);
        if (_valueLookup.TryGetValue(oldKey, out var existing) && ReferenceEquals(existing, item))
        {
            _valueLookup.Remove(oldKey);
        }

        _valueLookup[newValue] = item;
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Updates the shadow lookup when a registered shadow item's <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.Value"/> parameter changes.
    /// </summary>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Also requests a re-render of the parent <see cref="MudSelect{T}"/>: <c>GetSelectedValuePresenter</c> runs
    /// during the parent's render pass, before child <c>SetParametersAsync</c> has propagated the new value,
    /// so a second render is needed for the correct <see cref="MudSelectItem{T}.ChildContent"/> to be emitted.
    /// </remarks>
    public void OnShadowItemValueChanged(MudSelectItem<T> item, T? oldValue, T? newValue)
    {
        var oldKey = new NullableObject<T?>(oldValue);
        if (_shadowLookup.TryGetValue(oldKey, out var existing) && ReferenceEquals(existing, item))
        {
            _shadowLookup.Remove(oldKey);
        }

        _shadowLookup[newValue] = item;
        _select.InvalidateFitContent();
        ((IMudStateHasChanged)_select).StateHasChanged();
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Attempts to get an item by its value from visible items.
    /// </summary>
    public bool TryGetItemByValue(T? value, [NotNullWhen(true)] out MudSelectItem<T>? item)
    {
        return _valueLookup.TryGetValue(value, out item);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Attempts to get an item by its value from all items (including shadow items).
    /// </summary>
    public bool TryGetShadowItemByValue(T? value, [NotNullWhen(true)] out MudSelectItem<T>? item)
    {
        return _shadowLookup.TryGetValue(value, out item);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Subscribes to selection changes.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="observer">The callback to invoke when selection changes.</param>
    /// <returns>A disposable subscription that can be used to unsubscribe.</returns>
    public IDisposable SubscribeToSelectionChanges(Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
    {
        _selectionObservers.Add(observer);
        return new SelectionSubscription(this, observer);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Unsubscribes an observer from selection changes.
    /// </summary>
    private void Unsubscribe(Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
    {
        _selectionObservers.Remove(observer);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Notifies all observers of a selection change.
    /// </summary>
    public async Task NotifySelectionChangedAsync()
    {
        var selectedValues = SelectedValues;
        for (var i = _selectionObservers.Count - 1; i >= 0; i--)
        {
            await _selectionObservers[i](selectedValues);
        }
    }

    private sealed class SelectionSubscription(MudSelectContext<T> context, Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task> observer)
        : IDisposable
    {
        private MudSelectContext<T>? _context = context;
        private Func<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>, Task>? _observer = observer;

        public void Dispose()
        {
            var contextCopy = _context;
            var observerCopy = _observer;

            if (contextCopy is null || observerCopy is null)
            {
                return;
            }

            _context = null;
            _observer = null;

            contextCopy.Unsubscribe(observerCopy);
        }
    }
}
ENDOFFILE

Good. Now I also need to check if there are other places in `MudSelect.razor.cs` that need to use the custom comparer for lookups. Let me look at `MudSelect.razor.cs` more carefully for any issues.

Let me check the `SelectOption` method in `MudSelect.razor.cs`:

```csharp
public async Task SelectOption(T? value)
{
    var comparer = Comparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default;
    ...
    // Early exit if unchanged
    if (comparer.Equals(ReadValue, value))
    ...
}
```

This properly uses the custom comparer. Good.

Let me check `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync`:

```csharp
private async Task OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync(ParameterChangedEventArgs<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>?> arg)
{
    var value = arg.Value;
    _selectedValues = value != null ? new HashSet<T?>(value, Comparer) : new HashSet<T?>(Comparer);
    ...
    if (!MultiSelection)
    {
        await SetValueAndUpdateTextAsync(_selectedValues.FirstOrDefault());
    }
    ...
}
```

This properly creates the HashSet with the custom comparer. Good.

Now, there's another issue I need to consider. The `_selectedValues` field is a `HashSet<T?>` that's initialized as `new HashSet<T?>()` (without comparer). Let me check:

```csharp
private HashSet<T?> _selectedValues = [];
```

This uses the default comparer. But it gets overwritten in `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` with a new HashSet that uses the custom comparer. However, there might be other places that add to `_selectedValues` before it's properly initialized with a comparer.

Let me check where `_selectedValues` is modified:

1. In the field initializer: `private HashSet<T?> _selectedValues = [];`
2. In `OnComparerChangedAsync`: `_selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(_selectedValues, arg.Value);`
3. In `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync`: `_selectedValues = value != null ? new HashSet<T?>(value, Comparer) : new HashSet<T?>(Comparer);`
4. In `SelectOption`: `_selectedValues.Add(value)`, `_selectedValues.Remove(value)`, `_selectedValues.Clear()`
5. In `ClearAsync`: `_selectedValues.Clear()`
6. In `SelectAdjacentItem`: `_selectedValues.Clear(); _selectedValues.Add(item.Value);`
7. In `SelectAndHighlightItemAsync`: `_selectedValues.Clear(); _selectedValues.Add(item.Value);`
8. In `SelectLastItem`: `_selectedValues.Clear(); _selectedValues.Add(item.Value);`
9. In `SelectClearButtonClickHandlerAsync`: `_selectedValues.Clear()`
10. In `SelectAllItems`: `_selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(...)`

The issue is that `_selectedValues` is initialized without a comparer. If someone calls `SelectOption` before `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` is called (which sets the comparer), the operations on `_selectedValues` would use default equality.

But actually, looking at the constructor:

```csharp
registerScope.RegisterParameter<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>?>(nameof(SelectedValues))
    .WithParameter(() => SelectedValues)
    .WithEventCallback(() => SelectedValuesChanged)
    .WithChangeHandler(OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync)
    .WithComparer(() => new SequenceComparer<T?>(Comparer));
```

The `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` is called when `SelectedValues` changes. If `SelectedValues` is initially set to some values, this handler will be called during the first parameter set, which happens before any user interaction. So `_selectedValues` will be properly initialized with the custom comparer before any `SelectOption` calls.

But what if `SelectedValues` is not initially set (remains null/empty)? Then `_selectedValues` remains as `new HashSet<T?>()` without comparer. Then if the user selects an option, `SelectOption` is called, which adds to `_selectedValues`. The `Add` method of `HashSet<T?>` uses the comparer it was created with, which is `EqualityComparer<T?>.Default`. This could cause issues if the custom comparer is different from the default.

But wait, `SelectOption` itself creates a local `comparer` variable:

```csharp
var comparer = Comparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default;
```

But it only uses this for the early exit check. The actual `_selectedValues.Add(value)` uses the hash set's internal comparer.

So if `_selectedValues` was initialized without a comparer (when `SelectedValues` is null/empty), subsequent operations would not respect the custom comparer.

Let me fix this by initializing `_selectedValues` with a comparer-aware approach. Actually, since we can't access `Comparer` in the field initializer, we should initialize it in the constructor or in `OnInitialized`.

But actually, looking at the `OnComparerChangedAsync`:

```csharp
private async Task OnComparerChangedAsync(ParameterChangedEventArgs<IEqualityComparer<T?>?> arg)
{
    // Apply comparer and refresh selected values
    _selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(_selectedValues, arg.Value);
    await UpdateSelectedValuesStateAsync(arg.Value);
}
```

This is called when `Comparer` changes. It wraps `_selectedValues` in a new HashSet with the new comparer. But this is only called when `Comparer` changes, not when it's initially set.

Wait, actually, all parameter change handlers are called when parameters are first set. So `OnComparerChangedAsync` is called with the initial `Comparer` value. Let me check:

The `ParameterState` for `Comparer`:

```csharp
registerScope.RegisterParameter<IEqualityComparer<T?>?>(nameof(Comparer))
    .WithParameter(() => Comparer)
    .WithChangeHandler(OnComparerChangedAsync);
```

`OnComparerChangedAsync` is called whenever `Comparer` changes from its previous value. Initially, `Comparer` is `null`, and if the user sets it to a custom comparer, the handler is called. This would properly update `_selectedValues`.

But what if `Comparer` is set to a custom comparer initially and `SelectedValues` is also set initially? The order of parameter handlers matters. Let me check:

The `OnComparerChangedAsync` handler for `Comparer` and `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` for `SelectedValues` are both registered. The order they're called depends on the order they're registered. Looking at the constructor:

```csharp
registerScope.RegisterParameter<bool>(nameof(MultiSelection))
    ...
registerScope.RegisterParameter<IEqualityComparer<T?>?>(nameof(Comparer))
    .WithParameter(() => Comparer)
    .WithChangeHandler(OnComparerChangedAsync);
_openState = registerScope.RegisterParameter<bool>(nameof(Open))
    ...
_selectedValuesState = registerScope.RegisterParameter<IReadOnlyCollection<T?>?>(nameof(SelectedValues))
    .WithParameter(() => SelectedValues)
    .WithEventCallback(() => SelectedValuesChanged)
    .WithChangeHandler(OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync)
    .WithComparer(() => new SequenceComparer<T?>(Comparer));
```

So `Comparer` is registered before `SelectedValues`. If the handlers are called in registration order, `OnComparerChangedAsync` would be called before `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync`. That means:

1. `OnComparerChangedAsync` sets `_selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(_selectedValues, customComparer)`. But `_selectedValues` is currently empty, so it just creates an empty HashSet with the custom comparer.
2. `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` sets `_selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(value, Comparer)` using the custom comparer.

This should work correctly.

But what if `SelectedValues` is set but `Comparer` is not set (null)? Then `_selectedValues` uses default equality, which is correct because there's no custom comparer.

OK, I think the main fix is in `MudSelectContext`. But I should also fix the `_selectedValues` initialization to use the comparer from the start. However, since the comparer is not available in the field initializer, and the parameter handlers properly set it, it should be fine.

But wait, there's one more issue: `SelectOption` uses `_selectedValues.Add(value)` and `_selectedValues.Remove(value)`. If `_selectedValues` was initialized without a comparer (because `SelectedValues` is empty and `Comparer` is null), and later the user sets `Comparer` dynamically (after initial render), then `OnComparerChangedAsync` would wrap `_selectedValues` in a new HashSet with the custom comparer. But if the user then selects an option, the new HashSet would correctly use the custom comparer. However, if the user selected options before changing `Comparer`, those options would have been added with default equality, and after the comparer change, they'd be wrapped in a new HashSet. This should work because the new HashSet is constructed from the old one's elements, and the comparer is only used for subsequent operations.

But there's another edge case: what if `SelectedValues` is initially set with items, but `Comparer` is not set? Then `_selectedValues` is created with default comparer. Later, `Comparer` is set. `OnComparerChangedAsync` wraps `_selectedValues` in a new HashSet with the custom comparer. This is fine.

Now let me also think about the `MudSelect.razor.cs` file and see if there are other issues.

Let me look at the `CanRenderValue` property and `GetSelectedValuePresenter`:

```csharp
protected bool CanRenderValue
{
    get
    {
        if (MultiSelection)
        {
            return false;
        }
        if (ToStringFunc is not null && !string.IsNullOrEmpty(ToStringFunc(ReadValue)))
        {
            return false;
        }
        if (!_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue(ReadValue, out var item))
        {
            return false;
        }
        return item.ChildContent != null;
    }
}
```

And:

```csharp
protected RenderFragment? GetSelectedValuePresenter()
{
    if (!_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue(ReadValue, out var item))
    {
        return null;
    }
    return item.ChildContent;
}
```

Both use `_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue` which now uses the custom comparer. This should fix the issue where the input doesn't display anything.

This test doesn't use a custom comparer. Let me look for any test that tests initial values with a comparer. Since there isn't one, the bug might not be covered by existing tests.

Now let me think about whether my fix is complete. Let me trace through the scenario from the PR description:

**Scenario**: `MudSelect` has `Comparer` parameter set and it has some initial items in `SelectedValues` bound collection.

1. Component is created. Constructor sets `Comparer` = null (default).
2. `MudSelectContext` is created with `NullableObjectComparer` that reads from `_select.Comparer` (still null).
3. Parameters are set:
   - `Comparer` is set to custom comparer.
   - `OnComparerChangedAsync` is called: `_selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(_selectedValues, arg.Value)` - still empty.
   - `SelectedValues` is set to initial items.
   - `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` is called:
     - `_selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(value, Comparer)` - now has items with custom comparer.
     - For non-multi: `SetValueAndUpdateTextAsync(_selectedValues.FirstOrDefault())` sets the `Value`.
     - Calls `UpdateSelectedValuesStateAsync` which sets `_selectedValuesState` and notifies selection changes.
4. Render:
   - `MudSelectItem` components register themselves via `RegisterItem`.
   - `RegisterItem` adds to `_valueLookup` using the `NullableObjectComparer` which now uses the custom comparer.
   - `RegisterItem` checks if the item is selected using the custom comparer.
5. After render:
   - `CanRenderValue` is evaluated during rendering.
   - `_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue(ReadValue, out var item)` - this uses the dictionary with `NullableObjectComparer` which uses the custom comparer.
   - If the `ReadValue` is an object that is "equal" to a registered item's value via the custom comparer, the lookup succeeds.

This should work now!

But wait, there's an issue with `RegisterItem` calling `_select.GetSelectedValues()?.Contains(item.Value, comparer)`. The `GetSelectedValues()` returns `_selectedValuesState.Value`, which was set by `UpdateSelectedValuesStateAsync` to a `HashSet<T?>` with the custom comparer. The `Contains` with a comparer argument should work correctly. But note: `Contains(item.Value, comparer)` is an extension method that takes a comparer. Let me check if `HashSet<T>` has such a method... Actually, `Contains` with a comparer is an extension method from `System.Linq`:

```csharp
public static bool Contains<TSource>(this IEnumerable<TSource> source, TSource value, IEqualityComparer<TSource>? comparer);
```

This should work. But also, the `HashSet<T>` itself overrides `Contains(T)` to use its internal comparer. So even without the explicit comparer argument, it would work because the HashSet was created with the custom comparer.

However, in my edit to `RegisterItem`, I used `_select.GetSelectedValues()?.Contains(item.Value, comparer)`. The `GetSelectedValues()` returns `IReadOnlyCollection<T?>?`. The `Contains` with comparer is an extension method on `IEnumerable<T>`, so it should work.

But wait, there could be a problem: `GetSelectedValues()` might return `null`. Let me check:

```csharp
internal IReadOnlyCollection<T?>? GetSelectedValues() => _selectedValuesState.Value;
```

It can return null. In that case, the null-conditional operator `?.` would return null, and the `== true` check would fail, returning `false`. That's correct behavior.

Now, there's another subtle issue I noticed. In `RegisterItem`:

```csharp
_valueLookup[item.Value] = item;
```

This uses the dictionary's `NullableObjectComparer` which delegates to `_select.Comparer`. At the time of registration (during rendering), `_select.Comparer` should be set to the custom comparer. So the dictionary should use the correct comparer for both insertion and lookup.

But there's a potential problem with hash code stability. If the `Comparer` property changes after items are registered, the `NullableObjectComparer` would return different hash codes for the same keys, breaking the dictionary. However, as I said earlier, this is an edge case that's unlikely in practice. The `Comparer` is typically set once at initialization.

Let me also check if there's an issue with the `MudSelectItem`'s `OnSelectionChangedAsync`:

```csharp
private Task OnSelectionChangedAsync(IReadOnlyCollection<T?> selectedValues)
{
    var oldSelected = Selected;
    Selected = selectedValues.Contains(Value);
    ...
}
```

This uses `Contains` on `IReadOnlyCollection<T?>`. As I analyzed earlier, since the concrete type is `HashSet<T?>` (which implements `ICollection<T?>`), the LINQ `Contains` extension method will call `ICollection<T?>.Contains` which for `HashSet<T?>` uses its internal comparer (the custom one). So this should work correctly.

Now, let me also check if there's a problem with the `SelectOption` method's call to `_selectedValues.Add(value)`:

```csharp
public async Task SelectOption(T? value)
{
    var comparer = Comparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default;
    if (MultiSelection)
    {
        // Toggle selection
        if (!_selectedValues.Add(value))
        {
            _selectedValues.Remove(value);
        }
        ...
    }
    ...
}
```

If `_selectedValues` was initialized with the custom comparer (via `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` or `OnComparerChangedAsync`), then `Add` and `Remove` will use the custom comparer. But if neither `SelectedValues` nor `Comparer` was set, `_selectedValues` remains as `new HashSet<T?>()` without comparer. In that case, if the user later sets `Comparer` dynamically (not common), the `OnComparerChangedAsync` would wrap `_selectedValues` in a new HashSet with the custom comparer. But if `SelectOption` is called before `Comparer` is set, it would use default equality.

This is a pre-existing issue that's not part of the PR description. Let me focus on the main issue.

However, I should also fix the `_selectedValues` initialization to always use the available comparer. Let me look at how this can be done properly.

Actually, looking at the constructor:

```csharp
public MudSelect()
{
    _context = new MudSelectContext<T>(this);
    ...
}
```

The `Comparer` is not available yet. But we could change `_selectedValues` to be initialized later, in `OnInitialized` or `OnParametersSet`. However, that would be a bigger change.

A simpler approach: since the `Comparer` parameter change handler is always called before any user interaction, and it wraps `_selectedValues` in a new HashSet with the comparer, the only case where `_selectedValues` doesn't have the right comparer is when neither `Comparer` nor `SelectedValues` is set initially. But in that case, the default comparer is used, which is correct (because `Comparer` is null, so `Comparer ?? EqualityComparer<T?>.Default` = `EqualityComparer<T?>.Default`).

Wait, but what if `Comparer` is set but `SelectedValues` is not? Then:
1. `OnComparerChangedAsync` is called with the custom comparer.
2. `_selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(_selectedValues, arg.Value)` - creates empty HashSet with custom comparer.
3. `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` is not called because `SelectedValues` didn't change.
4. `_selectedValues` correctly has the custom comparer.

What if `SelectedValues` is set but `Comparer` is not?
1. `OnComparerChangedAsync` is not called (or called with null).
2. `OnSelectedValuesChangedAsync` is called with initial values.
3. `_selectedValues = new HashSet<T?>(value, Comparer)` where `Comparer` is null, so uses default equality.
4. Correct.

So the only edge case is when both are null/empty, in which case default equality is used, which is correct.

OK, I think the main fix is complete. But let me also check if there's another issue: the `MudSelect.razor.cs` uses `_context.TryGetShadowItemByValue` in several places, and I've fixed the dictionary to use the custom comparer. But what about `_context.TryGetItemByValue`? It's used in `HighlightItemForValueAsync`:

```csharp
private Task HighlightItemForValueAsync(T? value)
{
    _context.TryGetItemByValue(value, out var item);
    return HighlightItemAsync(item);
}
```

This now uses the fixed dictionary, so it should work.

Now let me double-check the `NullableObjectComparer` implementation. When the `Comparer` changes dynamically, the hash codes of keys already in the dictionary would change, which would break the dictionary. But as I said, this is an edge case. To handle it properly, we'd need to rebuild the dictionary when the comparer changes. Let me add that support.

I'll add a method to `MudSelectContext` that rebuilds the dictionaries, and call it from `MudSelect.OnComparerChangedAsync`.
